Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries\n\nThe **container manager** (`pkg/kubelet/cm`) is the kubelet's resource governance layer. Its core mandate is to enforce isolation and resource allocation for every process running on the node — from individual containers up to the node itself. It sits between the kubelet's pod-lifecycle orchestration and the Linux kernel's cgroup and CPU/memory topology subsystems.\n\n### What the container manager owns\n\n- **Cgroup hierarchy construction** — creates and maintains the `kubepods/`, `kubepods/burstable/`, and `kubepods/besteffort/` cgroups, plus per-pod sub-cgroups, mapping pod QoS classes to kernel resource controls.\n- **Node-level reservations** — enforces `kube-reserved` and `system-reserved` limits by placing kubelet processes and system daemons into dedicated cgroups with bounded resources.\n- **Extended resource allocation** — drives the device plugin protocol to advertise, allocate, and track hardware devices (GPUs, FPGAs, SR-IOV VFs, etc.) for containers.\n- **CPU and memory affinity** — co-ordinates exclusive CPU pinning and NUMA-local memory placement for Guaranteed pods.\n- **Topology-aware allocation** — ensures that CPUs, memory, and devices allocated to a container all reside on the same NUMA nodes.\n- **Dynamic Resource Allocation (DRA)** — manages `ResourceClaim` lifecycle for the structured device allocation API.\n- **Container lifecycle hooks** — injects resource assignments (cpusets, NUMA memsets) into the CRI container config immediately before container creation.\n\n### What it does not own\n\nThe container manager does not create containers (that is `kuberuntime`), does not schedule pods (that is the API server / scheduler), and does not perform eviction (that is `pkg/kubelet/eviction`). It exposes the `ContainerManager` interface (`pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager.go:66`) to the rest of the kubelet; everything else is internal.\n\n### Upstream dependencies\n\n| Dependency | Role |\n|---|---|\n| `cadvisor.Interface` | Machine topology discovery, rootfs/images filesystem sizes |\n| `cri-api RuntimeService` | UpdateContainerResources, container ID mapping |\n| `client-go clientset` | Watch/update `ResourceClaim` objects for DRA |\n| `pluginmanager` | Delivers plugin registration events to device manager and DRA |\n| `lifecycle.PodAdmitHandler` chain | Topology manager is injected here to gate pod admission |\n\n### Downstream dependencies\n\n| Downstream | How the CM interacts |\n|---|---|\n| Linux kernel cgroup v1/v2 | Direct filesystem writes via `opencontainers/cgroups` library |\n| CRI runtime (containerd, CRI-O) | `UpdateContainerResources` RPC for CPU set reconciliation |\n| Device plugins | gRPC over Unix socket, `pluginapi.v1beta1` |\n| DRA drivers | gRPC over Unix socket, `dra.v1` proto |\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibilities\n\n### 2.1 `ContainerManager` Interface\n\nDefined in `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager.go:66`. This is the single façade the kubelet uses. It exposes:\n- `Start(...)` — initialises all sub-managers and enforces node topology.\n- `GetResources(pod, container)` — collects device mounts, environment variables, and CDI devices needed to run a container.\n- `UpdatePluginResources(nodeInfo, attrs)` — triggers device plugin `Allocate()` during pod admission.\n- `GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler()` — returns the topology manager as an admit handler.\n- `InternalContainerLifecycle()` — returns the hook object called at each container lifecycle event.\n- `PrepareDynamicResources / UnprepareDynamicResources` — DRA claim prepare/unprepare.\n- `Updates() <-chan resourceupdates.Update` — fan-in channel carrying device-health and DRA status changes to the kubelet sync loop.\n\n### 2.2 `containerManagerImpl` (Linux)\n\nDefined in `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go:100`. The concrete Linux implementation holds references to all sub-managers:\n\n```\ncontainerManagerImpl\n├── cgroupManager      CgroupManager       (cgroup v1 or v2)\n├── qosContainerManager QOSContainerManager\n├── cpuManager         cpumanager.Manager\n├── memoryManager      memorymanager.Manager\n├── topologyManager    topologymanager.Manager\n├── deviceManager      devicemanager.Manager\n├── draManager         *dra.Manager\n└── resourceUpdates    chan resourceupdates.Update\n```\n\nWindows has a parallel `containerManagerImpl` in `container_manager_windows.go` that omits cgroup management but retains device manager, topology manager, CPU manager, and memory manager. A platform-agnostic stub (`container_manager_stub.go`) and an unsupported no-op (`container_manager_unsupported.go`) round out the platform variants.\n\n### 2.3 CgroupManager\n\n`pkg/kubelet/cm/cgroup_manager_linux.go` defines the `CgroupManager` interface. `NewCgroupManager()` (line 155) selects between `cgroupV1impl` and `cgroupV2impl` based on `cgroups.IsCgroup2UnifiedMode()`. Both embed `cgroupCommon`, which handles name translation between the kubelet's internal `CgroupName` type (a `[]string` path, e.g. `[\"kubepods\", \"burstable\", \"pod-abc\"]`) and the two external representations:\n\n- **cgroupfs** driver: `/kubepods/burstable/pod-abc`\n- **systemd** driver: `/kubepods.slice/kubepods-burstable.slice/kubepods-burstable-pod_abc.slice`\n\nThe name escaping rule is deterministic: `-` in pod UIDs becomes `_` in systemd names (`escapeSystemdCgroupName`, line 68), enabling lossless round-tripping. Underlying cgroup operations — `Create`, `Update`, `Destroy`, `Validate` — are delegated to the `opencontainers/cgroups/manager` library.\n\n### 2.4 QOS Container Manager\n\nManages the three top-level QoS cgroups (`Guaranteed`, `Burstable`, `BestEffort`) under the node-allocatable root. It periodically calls `UpdateCgroups()` to recompute CPU/memory limits from active pod totals, ensuring the top-level cgroups properly bound QoS classes.\n\n### 2.5 Pod Container Manager\n\nReturned by `NewPodContainerManager()` (line 397 of `container_manager_linux.go`). When `CgroupsPerQOS` is enabled it creates `podContainerManagerImpl`; otherwise it returns `podContainerManagerNoop`. The impl creates per-pod cgroups (`/kubepods/burstable/pod<uid>/`) and translates `ResourceConfig` (CPU shares, quota, memory limit, hugepage limits) into cgroup writes via `CgroupManager`.\n\n`ResourceConfigForPod()` (`helpers_linux.go:126`) is the arithmetic engine: it converts pod `requests`/`limits` into CFS shares (`MilliCPUToShares`) and CFS quota (`MilliCPUToQuota`), differentiating by QoS class — Guaranteed pods get both shares and quota; BestEffort pods receive only `MinShares = 2`.\n\n### 2.6 CPU Manager\n\n`pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/cpu_manager.go`. Provides exclusive CPU pinning for Guaranteed pods with integer CPU requests.\n\n**Policies** (selected by `--cpu-manager-policy`):\n\n| Policy | Behaviour |\n|---|---|\n| `none` (default) | No pinning; all containers share all CPUs via cgroup `cpuset.cpus`. |\n| `static` | Exclusively allocates whole CPUs to eligible containers. Maintains three sets: RESERVED (system+kube reserved, never exclusively assigned), SHARED (burstable/besteffort pool), and EXCLUSIVE ALLOCATIONS (per-container pinned sets). |\n\nThe `static` policy (`policy_static.go:108`) reads the NUMA topology from cAdvisor's `MachineInfo`, accepts the topology manager's affinity hint before allocating, and calls `state.SetCPUSet()` to persist the assignment. A periodic `reconcileState()` goroutine (started at `cpu_manager.go:255`) calls `runtimeService.UpdateContainerResources()` to push the current cpuset to containers that may have drifted — for example after a container restart.\n\nState is checkpointed to `<kubelet-root>/cpu_manager_state` (a JSON file written via `checkpointmanager`), so allocations survive kubelet restarts.\n\n### 2.7 Memory Manager\n\n`pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/memory_manager.go`. Manages NUMA-local memory placement for Guaranteed pods. Mirrors the CPU manager's structure: a `Manager` interface, a `Policy` interface, a `none` policy and a `static` policy. The static policy pins `cpuset.mems` (the NUMA memory nodes) for eligible containers. State is checkpointed to `<kubelet-root>/memory_manager_state`.\n\n### 2.8 Topology Manager\n\n`pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/topology_manager.go`. Acts as a cross-resource NUMA alignment broker. It implements `lifecycle.PodAdmitHandler`, so it is registered in the kubelet's pod-admit chain (`kubelet.go:1064`).\n\n**Scope** (per-container or per-pod, `scope.go`): determines whether alignment is computed per container or across all containers in a pod simultaneously.\n\n**Policies** (selected by `--topology-manager-policy`):\n\n| Policy | Behaviour |\n|---|---|\n| `none` | Calls `Allocate()` on each hint provider without checking alignment. |\n| `best-effort` | Attempts aligned allocation; admits the pod regardless. |\n| `restricted` | Requires at least one aligned hint; rejects if none found. |\n| `single-numa-node` | Requires all resources on a single NUMA node; rejects otherwise. |\n\nWhen a pod is admitted, the scope calls `GetTopologyHints()` on each registered `HintProvider` (CPU manager, memory manager, device manager — all implement `HintProvider`). Each provider returns a list of `TopologyHint{NUMANodeAffinity bitmask.BitMask, Preferred bool}`. The topology manager intersects these hint sets to find the best (narrowest) aligned bitmask and stores it in its `Store`. Hint providers subsequently query `store.GetAffinity()` during their own `Allocate()` calls to honour the consensus.\n\nThe maximum supported NUMA node count is 8 (`defaultMaxAllowableNUMANodes = 8`, line 41), because the hint-intersection algorithm is exponential in the number of NUMA nodes.\n\n### 2.9 Device Manager\n\n`pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/manager.go`. The `ManagerImpl` struct maintains a map of `endpoints` keyed by resource name (e.g. `nvidia.com/gpu`). Each endpoint wraps a gRPC connection to a device plugin. The manager:\n\n1. Receives plugin registrations from the plugin watcher via `GetWatcherHandler()`.\n2. Calls `ListAndWatch()` on each plugin to maintain `healthyDevices` and `unhealthyDevices` sets.\n3. At pod admission, calls `Allocate()` on the appropriate plugin and stores the result (`devices`, `mounts`, `envs`, `CDIDevices`) in `podDevices`.\n4. Serves `GetDeviceRunContainerOptions()` at container creation time to supply that stored state to `GetResources()`.\n\nDevice allocations are checkpointed to `<kubelet-root>/device-plugins/` via `checkpointmanager`. The manager exposes a health checker used by the kubelet's `/healthz` endpoint.\n\n### 2.10 DRA Manager\n\n`pkg/kubelet/cm/dra/manager.go`. Implements the structured Dynamic Resource Allocation API (gated by the `DynamicResourceAllocation` feature gate). Its responsibilities:\n\n- Manages `ResourceClaim` prepare/unprepare via DRA driver plugins registered through the plugin watcher.\n- Checkpoints claim state to `<kubelet-root>/dra_manager_state` for recovery across kubelet restarts.\n- Publishes health-status updates to the `update` channel (consumed by the kubelet when `ResourceHealthStatus` feature gate is on).\n- Runs a periodic reconcile loop (`defaultReconcilePeriod = 60s`) to clean up stale claims.\n\n### 2.11 `InternalContainerLifecycle`\n\nDefined in `pkg/kubelet/cm/internal_container_lifecycle.go:28`. This interface bridges the container manager to `kuberuntime`:\n\n```go\ntype InternalContainerLifecycle interface {\n    PreCreateContainer(logger, pod, container, containerConfig) error\n    PreStartContainer(logger, pod, container, containerID) error\n    PostStopContainer(logger, containerID) error\n}\n```\n\nThe implementation (`internalContainerLifecycleImpl`) holds references to the CPU manager, memory manager, and topology manager. The three hooks are called in order by `kuberuntime_container.go` during each container's create/start/stop sequence.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Control Flow\n\n### 3.1 Startup\n\n```\nkubelet.Run()\n  └─ containerManager.Start(ctx, node, activePods, getNode, sourcesReady, statusManager, runtimeService, ...)\n       ├─ buildContainerMapAndRunningSetFromRuntime()   # enumerate live containers from CRI\n       ├─ draManager.Start()                            # if DRAFeatureGate enabled\n       ├─ cpuManager.Start()                            # loads checkpoint, starts reconcile goroutine\n       ├─ memoryManager.Start()                         # loads checkpoint, starts reconcile goroutine\n       ├─ validateNodeAllocatable()\n       ├─ setupNode()\n       │    ├─ validateSystemRequirements()             # verifies required cgroup subsystems are mounted\n       │    ├─ setupKernelTunables()                    # vm.overcommit_memory, kernel.panic, etc.\n       │    ├─ createNodeAllocatableCgroups()           # creates /kubepods cgroup\n       │    ├─ qosContainerManager.Start()              # creates Guaranteed/Burstable/BestEffort cgroups\n       │    └─ ensureNodeAllocatableCgroups()           # sets resource limits on /kubepods\n       └─ deviceManager.Start()                         # starts ListAndWatch for all registered plugins\n```\n\n`container_manager_linux.go:615`\n\n### 3.2 Pod Admission\n\nPod admission runs before any container is created. The topology manager acts as the first admit handler (`kubelet.go:1064`):\n\n```\ntopologyManager.Admit(pod)\n  └─ scope.Admit()\n       ├─ for each container:\n       │    ├─ cpuManager.GetTopologyHints(pod, container)\n       │    ├─ memoryManager.GetTopologyHints(pod, container)\n       │    └─ deviceManager.GetTopologyHints(pod, container)\n       ├─ policy.Merge(allHints) → best TopologyHint\n       ├─ scope.setTopologyHints(podUID, containerName, hint)\n       └─ for each container:\n            ├─ cpuManager.Allocate(pod, container)      # reserves CPUs in checkpoint\n            ├─ memoryManager.Allocate(pod, container)   # reserves NUMA memory blocks\n            └─ deviceManager.Allocate(pod, container)   # calls plugin Allocate(), stores result\n```\n\nThe second admit handler (`kubelet.go:1067`) is `lifecycle.NewPredicateAdmitHandler`, which calls `containerManager.UpdatePluginResources()` to ensure the node's `allocatableResource` reflects any device plugin resource that was just allocated.\n\n### 3.3 Container Creation\n\n`kuberuntime_container.go` calls the container manager at three points around each CRI `CreateContainer`/`StartContainer` call:\n\n```\nkuberuntime.createContainer(pod, container)\n  ├─ containerManager.GetResources(pod, container)\n  │    ├─ draManager.GetResources()       → CDI device list\n  │    └─ deviceManager.GetDeviceRunContainerOptions()  → mounts, envs, CDI devices\n  │\n  ├─ (build CRI ContainerConfig)\n  │\n  ├─ internalLifecycle.PreCreateContainer(logger, pod, container, containerConfig)\n  │    ├─ cpuManager.GetCPUAffinity()     → sets containerConfig.Linux.Resources.CpusetCpus\n  │    └─ memoryManager.GetMemoryNUMANodes() → sets containerConfig.Linux.Resources.CpusetMems\n  │         (linux-only, internal_container_lifecycle_linux.go:31)\n  │\n  ├─ runtimeService.CreateContainer(containerConfig)   → containerID\n  │\n  ├─ internalLifecycle.PreStartContainer(logger, pod, container, containerID)\n  │    ├─ cpuManager.AddContainer()       → registers containerID → (podUID, containerName)\n  │    ├─ memoryManager.AddContainer()    → same\n  │    └─ topologyManager.AddContainer()  → tracks containerID in scope podMap\n  │\n  └─ runtimeService.StartContainer(containerID)\n```\n\n### 3.4 Container Removal\n\n```\nkuberuntime.killContainer() / removeContainer()\n  └─ internalLifecycle.PostStopContainer(logger, containerID)\n       └─ topologyManager.RemoveContainer(containerID)\n            ├─ cpuManager.RemoveContainer()     → frees exclusive CPUs back to shared pool\n            └─ memoryManager.RemoveContainer()  → frees NUMA memory blocks\n```\n\n`kuberuntime_container.go:1360`, `kuberuntime_manager.go:1245`\n\n### 3.5 Resource Updates\n\nDevice plugins and DRA drivers can report device health changes asynchronously. `containerManagerImpl` fans these in through goroutines started in `NewContainerManager()` (`container_manager_linux.go:363`):\n\n```go\nsources[\"deviceManager\"] = cm.deviceManager.Updates()\nsources[\"draManager\"]    = cm.draManager.Updates()\n// fan-in to cm.resourceUpdates\n```\n\nThe kubelet consumes `containerManager.Updates()` in its main sync loop to trigger pod status reconciliation (e.g. to surface device health conditions).\n\n---\n\n## 4. Platform Variance\n\n| Feature | Linux (cgroupv2) | Linux (cgroupv1) | Windows | Unsupported |\n|---|---|---|---|---|\n| Cgroup hierarchy | Full (`cgroupV2impl`) | Full (`cgroupV1impl`) | None | None |\n| QoS cgroups | Yes | Yes | No | No |\n| CPU manager | Yes (none/static) | Yes (none/static) | Yes (none/static) | No |\n| Memory manager | Yes | Yes | Yes | No |\n| Device manager | Yes | Yes | Yes | No |\n| Topology manager | Yes | Yes | Yes | No |\n| DRA manager | Yes | Yes | No (windows excluded) | No |\n| Kernel tunable setup | Yes | Yes | No | No |\n| CPU hard-capping | Yes (always) | Conditional on `cpu.cfs_quota_us` | No | No |\n\n**cgroupv1 deprecation**: The `CgroupV1DeprecatedWarning` constant (`container_manager.go:52`) is surfaced in kubelet startup logs. cgroupv1 support is explicitly scheduled for removal in a future release.\n\n**Windows**: The `containerManagerImpl` in `container_manager_windows.go` holds the device manager, topology manager, CPU manager, and memory manager, but has no `cgroupManager` or `qosContainerManager` field. `Start()` only initialises the device manager. DRA is excluded by a build constraint comment.\n\n**User namespace**: `container_manager_linux.go:491` uses `inuserns.RunningInUserNS()` to detect user-namespace execution and suppresses sysctl errors when the `KubeletInUserNamespace` feature gate is set, enabling kubelet-in-container test environments.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Failure Modes and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 5.1 Startup Failures\n\n- Missing cgroup subsystems (`cpu`, `cpuacct`, `cpuset`, `memory`) are hard errors on cgroupv1. The kubelet will not start (`validateSystemRequirements`, `container_manager_linux.go:151`).\n- Swap enabled with `--fail-swap-on=true` (default) aborts startup. With swap on and tmpfs noswap unsupported, the kubelet emits a `PossibleMemoryBackedVolumesOnDisk` warning event but continues.\n- Invalid `cgroup-root` (path must exist on the filesystem) is a hard startup error.\n\n### 5.2 CPU Manager Policy Conflicts\n\n- The `static` policy requires `kube-reserved.cpu + system-reserved.cpu > 0`. If reserved CPUs are zero, the manager refuses to start (`cpu_manager.go:194`).\n- SMT topology mismatches are surfaced as `SMTAlignmentError` during pod admission, not at startup.\n- Checkpoint corruption (e.g. after a policy name change) causes the CPU manager to log an error and drain the node (`cpu_manager.go:234`): _\"please drain node and remove policy state file\"_.\n\n### 5.3 Topology Manager Admission Failures\n\n- With `restricted` or `single-numa-node` policy, pods that cannot be NUMA-aligned will fail admission with a `TopologyAffinityError`. This is a hard rejection; the kubelet will never start the pod without operator intervention (policy change or pod removal).\n- The 8-NUMA-node limit is a deliberate algorithmic cap: hint intersection is exponential in node count, and beyond 8 nodes the state space is considered too large to enumerate safely.\n\n### 5.4 Device Plugin Failures\n\n- A device plugin that disconnects is removed from the active endpoint list. Pods already using those devices continue to run (allocations are in the checkpoint), but new pods cannot be admitted for that resource.\n- `ShouldResetExtendedResourceCapacity()` (`container_manager_linux.go:1068`) detects node recreation (by comparing a fingerprint file) and returns `true`, causing the kubelet to zero out device plugin resource capacities on the node object. This prevents scheduling pods to a node that has lost its device plugin state.\n\n### 5.5 Reconciliation Drift\n\nThe CPU manager's periodic `reconcileState()` covers the window between when a cpuset is assigned in memory and when `UpdateContainerResources` reaches the runtime. If the runtime is temporarily unavailable, the reconciler retries on the next period. During this window, a container's actual cpuset in the kernel may not match the desired assignment.\n\n### 5.6 Cgroup v1/v2 Behavioural Differences\n\n- **CPU shares vs. CPU weight**: cgroupv2 uses `cpu.weight` (range 1–10000); cgroupv1 uses `cpu.shares` (range 2–262144). `getCPUWeight()` in `cgroup_manager_linux.go:267` converts between them with a linear mapping.\n- **Memory QoS**: cgroupv2 adds `memory.min` (guaranteed minimum) and `memory.high` (soft throttle) in addition to `memory.limit_in_bytes`. The `Cgroup2MemoryMin` and `Cgroup2MemoryHigh` constants (`cgroup_manager_linux.go:43`) are written as `Unified` resource parameters in `ResourceConfig`.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Extension Points and Customisation Hooks\n\n### 6.1 CPU Manager Policy Options\n\nThe `static` policy supports fine-grained options passed via `--cpu-manager-policy-options`:\n\n- `full-pcpus-only`: Require that exclusive allocations align to full physical CPU cores (prevents hyper-thread splitting).\n- `distribute-cpus-across-numa`: Spread exclusive CPUs across multiple NUMA nodes rather than packing them.\n- `align-by-socket`: Align allocations to CPU socket boundaries.\n\nOptions are validated at startup in `NewStaticPolicyOptions()` (`pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/policy_options.go`). Unknown options cause a startup error, preventing silent misconfiguration.\n\n### 6.2 Topology Manager Policy and Scope\n\nBoth `--topology-manager-policy` and `--topology-manager-scope` are runtime-configurable. The scope determines whether the hint-intersection considers each container independently (`container` scope, `scope_container.go`) or treats all containers in a pod as a single allocation unit (`pod` scope, `scope_pod.go`). The `pod` scope is necessary when containers within a pod share devices and must be co-located on the same NUMA node.\n\n### 6.3 Device Plugin Registration\n\nThird-party device plugins register by creating a Unix socket at `/var/lib/kubelet/device-plugins/<name>.sock`. The plugin watcher (`pkg/kubelet/pluginmanager`) delivers registration events to `deviceManager.GetWatcherHandler()`. This is the primary hardware extension point: any resource that can be represented as a set of opaque device IDs with NUMA affinity can be integrated without modifying kubelet source.\n\n### 6.4 DRA Drivers\n\nDRA drivers register via a separate socket path and implement the `dra.v1` gRPC protocol. Unlike device plugins, DRA allocations are API-server-mediated: the scheduler allocates `ResourceClaims`, and the kubelet's DRA manager calls `NodePrepareResources` / `NodeUnprepareResources` on the driver to make devices available inside the pod's namespaces (via CDI device IDs). This decoupling means DRA can support more complex allocation models (e.g. sharing a device across pods, network fabric allocation) that device plugins cannot express.\n\n**Risk**: DRA drivers run as privileged processes on the node and have the ability to inject arbitrary CDI device specifications (`opts.CDIDevices`, `container_manager_linux.go:737`). A compromised driver can inject devices into any pod. Cluster operators must treat DRA driver deployment with the same trust level as node-level privilege.\n\n### 6.5 QOS Reserved Percentages\n\n`ParseQOSReserved()` (`container_manager.go:267`) allows operators to reserve a percentage of memory for the QoS cgroup tiers via `--qos-reserved`. Only `memory` is supported. This enables over-commitment headroom reservation at the cgroup level independent of pod requests.\n\n### 6.6 `InternalContainerLifecycle` as an Internal Hook\n\n`InternalContainerLifecycle` is not a public extension point — it is an internal interface (`pkg/kubelet/cm`) consumed only by `kuberuntime`. However, it is the mechanism by which any new resource manager that needs to inject configuration into CRI `ContainerConfig` should register. Adding a new resource manager that influences container startup requires:\n\n1. Implementing `HintProvider` and registering with the topology manager.\n2. Storing allocation state in the manager.\n3. Reading that state in `PreCreateContainer` to modify `containerConfig`.\n4. Registering/deregistering the container in `PreStartContainer` / `PostStopContainer`.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Operational Implications\n\n### 7.1 Performance\n\n**Reconcile period tuning** (`--cpu-manager-reconcile-period`, default 10 s): Each reconcile period triggers an `UpdateContainerResources` RPC for every active container that has a tracked CPU assignment. On nodes with many containers, a short reconcile period increases CRI load. Widening the period increases the drift window between assignment and enforcement after container restarts.\n\n**Topology hint computation cost**: The hint-intersection algorithm in `scope_container.go` / `scope_pod.go` is O(product of hint counts). With the default max of 8 NUMA nodes and multiple hint providers, this is bounded to a few thousand operations per admission and is not a practical bottleneck. However, device plugins that return a large number of fine-grained hints (one hint per device rather than per-NUMA-node aggregation) can expand the search space significantly.\n\n**Cgroup write latency**: Every pod creation issues at least one `cgroupManager.Create()` and one `cgroupManager.Update()` call. Under the systemd driver, these are mediated by D-Bus RPC to systemd, which serialises cgroup operations on slow nodes. Operators on high-density nodes (hundreds of pods/min) may see admission latency dominated by systemd D-Bus round-trips.\n\n### 7.2 Reliability\n\n**Checkpoint files** are the critical recovery artefact. The kubelet stores three checkpoint files under `<kubelet-root>`:\n- `cpu_manager_state`\n- `memory_manager_state`\n- `device-plugins/<checkpoint>`\n\nThese are written atomically via `checkpointmanager`. If they are deleted while the kubelet is stopped, the manager will reconstruct state by querying the CRI for live containers on next start. If the files are corrupted or represent a previous policy name, a hard startup error is surfaced. The recommended recovery procedure is to drain the node and remove the state file before changing policies.\n\n**Policy change**: Changing `--cpu-manager-policy` between `none` and `static` requires draining the node first. The checkpoint format encodes the policy name; a mismatch is detected at startup and blocks the node from accepting new pods until resolved.\n\n### 7.3 Maintainability\n\nThe subsystem uses the **strategy pattern** consistently: `CgroupManager`, `Policy` (CPU/memory), and `Scope` (topology) are all interfaces with multiple concrete implementations. This makes unit-testing straightforward — `fake_container_manager.go`, `fake_cpu_manager.go`, `fake_memory_manager.go`, and `fake_topology_manager.go` all provide stub implementations used by the kubelet's own test suite.\n\nPlatform variance is handled through Go build tags (`//go:build linux`, `//go:build windows`) rather than runtime switches. Each platform file declares its own `containerManagerImpl` struct with only the fields applicable to that OS. This eliminates nil-check guards throughout the codebase but requires that any new feature be explicitly ported to each platform or left as a no-op in the unsupported file.\n\n---\n\n## 8. File and Directory Map\n\n```\npkg/kubelet/cm/\n│\n├── container_manager.go              # ContainerManager interface, NodeConfig, NodeAllocatableConfig\n├── container_manager_linux.go        # containerManagerImpl (Linux): Start(), GetResources(), ...\n├── container_manager_windows.go      # containerManagerImpl (Windows): partial implementation\n├── container_manager_unsupported.go  # No-op for non-Linux/Windows platforms\n├── container_manager_stub.go         # Test stub; NewStubContainerManager()\n│\n├── cgroup_manager_linux.go           # CgroupManager interface, cgroupCommon, NewCgroupManager()\n├── cgroup_v1_manager_linux.go        # cgroupV1impl: Create/Update/Destroy for cgroup v1\n├── cgroup_v2_manager_linux.go        # cgroupV2impl: Create/Update/Destroy for cgroup v2\n├── cgroup_manager_unsupported.go     # Stub for non-Linux builds\n│\n├── helpers.go                        # Cross-platform helpers\n├── helpers_linux.go                  # ResourceConfigForPod(), MilliCPUToShares(), MilliCPUToQuota()\n│                                     # GetCgroupSubsystems(), getCgroupSubsystemsV1/V2()\n│\n├── internal_container_lifecycle.go             # InternalContainerLifecycle interface\n├── internal_container_lifecycle_linux.go       # PreCreateContainer: writes cpusetCpus, cpusetMems\n├── internal_container_lifecycle_windows.go     # Windows PreCreateContainer (CPU manager only)\n├── internal_container_lifecycle_unsupported.go # No-ops\n│\n├── admission/errors.go               # Admission failure error types\n│\n├── containermap/container_map.go     # ContainerMap: (podUID, containerName) <-> containerID index\n│\n├── cpumanager/\n│   ├── cpu_manager.go                # Manager interface, manager struct, Start/Allocate/Reconcile\n│   ├── policy.go                     # Policy interface\n│   ├── policy_none.go                # NonePolicy: no-op allocator\n│   ├── policy_static.go              # StaticPolicy: exclusive CPU allocation logic\n│   ├── policy_options.go             # StaticPolicyOptions parsing and validation\n│   ├── state/\n│   │   ├── state.go                  # Reader/State interfaces\n│   │   ├── state_checkpoint.go       # Persistent checkpoint state\n│   │   └── state_mem.go              # In-memory state (used for lastUpdateState)\n│   └── topology/\n│       ├── topology.go               # CPUTopology: Discover() from cAdvisor MachineInfo\n│       └── alignment.go              # NUMA alignment helpers\n│\n├── memorymanager/\n│   ├── memory_manager.go             # Manager interface, manager struct\n│   ├── policy_static.go              # StaticPolicy: NUMA memory block allocation\n│   ├── policy_none.go                # NonePolicy: no-op\n│   └── state/                        # Checkpoint state (same pattern as cpumanager/state)\n│\n├── topologymanager/\n│   ├── topology_manager.go           # Manager interface, HintProvider interface, TopologyHint\n│   ├── scope.go                      # Scope interface and common scope struct\n│   ├── scope_container.go            # Per-container admit logic\n│   ├── scope_pod.go                  # Per-pod admit logic\n│   ├── policy.go                     # Policy interface\n│   ├── policy_none.go                # None: no alignment enforcement\n│   ├── policy_best_effort.go         # BestEffort: align if possible\n│   ├── policy_restricted.go          # Restricted: require alignment\n│   └── policy_single_numa_node.go    # SingleNUMANode: require single-node\n│\n├── devicemanager/\n│   ├── manager.go                    # ManagerImpl: endpoint map, ListAndWatch, Allocate\n│   ├── pod_devices.go                # podDevices: allocation tracking per (pod, container)\n│   ├── checkpoint/checkpoint.go      # Checkpoint format for device allocations\n│   ├── topology_hints.go             # GetTopologyHints() for device manager\n│   └── plugin/v1beta1/               # gRPC client/server for device plugin protocol\n│\n├── dra/\n│   ├── manager.go                    # DRA Manager: PrepareResources/UnprepareResources\n│   ├── claiminfo.go                  # ClaimInfo: in-memory state per ResourceClaim\n│   ├── healthinfo.go                 # HealthInfo: device health tracking\n│   ├── state/                        # Persistent checkpoint for DRA claim state\n│   └── plugin/                       # DRA driver plugin gRPC client\n│\n└── resourceupdates/                  # Update type: set of pod UIDs affected by a resource change\n```\n\n---\n\n## 9. Summary\n\nThe kubelet container manager is a layered resource governance subsystem built around a single `ContainerManager` interface that the kubelet calls at node startup, pod admission, container create/start/stop, and resource query time. On Linux, the concrete implementation orchestrates six interdependent sub-managers — cgroup, QoS, CPU, memory, device, and DRA — through a well-defined interface hierarchy where the topology manager acts as the admission-time arbiter ensuring cross-resource NUMA alignment. The `InternalContainerLifecycle` hook is the concrete integration point with `kuberuntime`, injecting CPU and memory affinity into CRI `ContainerConfig` immediately before each container is created. On Windows the subsystem is narrower (no cgroup management) but structurally parallel. The subsystem's primary operational risks are checkpoint file hygiene during policy changes, device plugin trust boundaries, and the hard limit of 8 NUMA nodes for topology alignment.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
